## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of nonlinear second-order oscillators. Common structures include restoring forces (linear or nonlinear in x), damping (linear or nonlinear in v and/or x), and external periodic forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; c0 typically negative)
- Linear damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (spring + viscous damping; c0<0, c1<0)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (periodic external forcing)
- Coulomb (dry) friction model: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sign(v) (restoring + velocity-sign friction; piecewise via sign)
- Quadratic (turbulent) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag magnitude grows with speed squared)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (canonical nonlinear forced oscillator)
- Higher-order stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger amplitude-dependent restoring force)
- Pendulum (nonlinear sine restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(x) + c1 * v (small-angle limit recovers linear SHO; damping optional)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x| → limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (self-excited oscillations via nonlinear damping)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type behavior)
- Nonlinear coupling drag/stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- General polynomial normal form (odd restoring + damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v + c4 * v**3 (common symbolic-regression search space for nonlinear oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about x=0, restoring terms in dv_dt are often odd in x (x, x**3, x**5, sin(x)); even-in-x terms can indicate asymmetry or bias.
- Conservative vs dissipative signature: purely x-dependent dv_dt suggests conservative dynamics; any explicit v-dependence typically introduces dissipation or self-excitation.
- Linear damping identification: a dominant term proportional to v indicates viscous damping; the sign of its coefficient determines energy loss (negative) vs active gain (positive).
- Nonlinear damping identification: v*Abs(v) suggests quadratic drag; v**3 terms suggest Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping; (c - x**2)*v suggests van der Pol–type state-dependent damping and limit cycles.
- Hardening/softening stiffness: inclusion of x**3 (and higher odd powers) indicates amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening if coefficient sign matches linear stiffness, softening if opposite).
- Pendulum-like behavior: sin(x) structure implies bounded restoring acceleration for large |x| and reduces to linear c*x for small |x|.
- External periodic forcing: explicit cos(c*t + phi) or sin(c*t + phi) terms in dv_dt indicate driven oscillations, resonance, and possibly chaotic regimes when combined with nonlinear stiffness.
- Parametric excitation cue: time-periodic modulation multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) signals Mathieu/parametric resonance rather than additive forcing.
- Energy-balance intuition: terms that scale strongly with |v| (v*Abs(v), v**3) dominate at high speeds and can clamp amplitudes or shape limit-cycle amplitude.
- State-space consistency check: physically plausible dv_dt typically depends on x and v (and sometimes t) but not on derivatives; overly complex explicit t-polynomials often indicate fitting artifacts unless parameters truly drift in time.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO17)

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
0.4607662803\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.2634379499\,v\sin(x)\;-\;0.5268758999\,v\;-\;2.5071295689\,x.
\]
So GT contains exactly these structures: \(\sin(t)\), \(v\sin(x)\), \(v\), and \(x\). No constants, no \(vx\), no \(vx^2\), no exponentials/logs, no piecewise Max/Abs terms.

A candidate can match only if it can be parameter-set to **exactly** those four terms and nothing else, and it must be able to represent \(v\sin(x)\) (not \(vx\), not \(v e^{kx}\), etc.).

Also, \(\cos(t+\phi)\) can match \(\sin(t)\) by phase shift: \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin(t)\). So any candidate with a cosine-in-\(t\) term can represent the forcing term.

---

### 1
Has Max(0,±v), \(vx\), \(vx^2\), \(v e^{c x}\), plus fixed extra \(+v + x\) (not parameterized). Those fixed \(+v\) and \(+x\) force coefficients 1 on \(v\) and \(x\), but GT needs \(-0.5268...\) and \(-2.5071...\). No way to remove/adjust them (unless other terms cancel, but there is no plain \(-v\) or \(-x\) knob independent of \(x\) or \(v\) besides \(c7 x\) and maybe \(c0 v\) etc—here only \(c7 x\) exists but still leaves the fixed \(+x\)). Also cannot create \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 2
Has \(\cos(t+\phi)\) (good for \(\sin t\)), has plain \(x\) via \(c2 x\) and \(c7 x\) (can combine), has \(vx\), \(vx^2\), \(v e^{cx}\), and a fixed \(+v\) with coefficient 1 (not adjustable). GT needs coefficient \(-0.5268...\) on \(v\), so you’d need another plain \(v\) term to adjust; none exists. Also cannot form \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 3
Has plain \(v\) (good), \(\cos(t+\phi)\) (good), plain \(x\) (good), but the only \(x\)-dependent \(v\) term is \(v x\), \(v x^2\), \(v e^{cx}\), \(v x^2|v|\). None can equal \(v\sin(x)\) for all \(x\). **No match.**

### 4
Has fixed \(+v + x\) again (wrong fixed coefficients), and only \(vx, vx^2, v e^{cx}\) for coupling. No \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 5
Has \(\cos(t+\phi)\), constant \(c2\) (GT has no constant so must set \(c2=0\)), has \(v\) via \(c3 v\) plus fixed \(+v\) (so coefficient is \(c3+1\), adjustable), has \(x\) via \(c4 x\) and \(c9 x\) (adjustable). But coupling is \(vx, vx^2, v e^{cx}\), not \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 6
Includes extra term \(x/(c9+|x|)^3\) which cannot be made identically zero by parameter choice unless \(c8=0\) (ok). Still lacks \(v\sin(x)\); has fixed \(+v\) coefficient 1 again (no other plain \(v\) term), so cannot match \(-0.5268...\). **No match.**

### 7
Has constant \(c8\) (must be 0), has fixed \(+v\) coefficient 1 (no other plain \(v\)), so cannot match \(v\) coefficient. Also no \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 8
Has fixed \(+v\) coefficient 1 (no other plain \(v\)), so cannot match \(v\) coefficient. No \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 9
Has fixed \(+v + x + \text{Max}(0,v)\) and Max(0,-v). Those piecewise terms cannot combine to a pure linear \(v\) for all \(v\) unless you use identity \(v=\max(0,v)-\max(0,-v)\), but there is already a fixed \(+v\) and fixed \(+\max(0,v)\) with coefficient 1, making it impossible to tune to a single linear coefficient for all \(v\) without leftover piecewise parts. Also no \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 10
Has \(\cos(t+\phi)\), \(x\) terms, constant \(c8\) (set 0), and fixed \(+v\) coefficient 1 (no other plain \(v\)) so cannot match \(v\) coefficient. No \(v\sin(x)\). **No match.**

### 11

Core obstruction across all candidates: none contains a term of the form \(v\sin(x)\) (or an exactly equivalent representation allowing phase shift in \(x\), e.g., \(v\cos(x+\phi)\)). The only \(x\)-dependent \(v\) terms offered are polynomials in \(x\), exponentials, logs, powers, or cosine without phase in \(x\); these cannot equal \(\sin(x)\) for all real \(x\). Therefore no candidate can be made identical to the GT for all \((x,t,v)\).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO17)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.263437949946663*v*sin(x) - 0.526875899893326*v - 2.50712956886133*x + 0.460766280298364*sin(t)`

Key terms in GT:
1. `sin(t)` term
2. `v*sin(x)` term
3. `v` term (linear in v)
4. `x` term (linear in x)

The critical feature is the `v*sin(x)` term. This is a product of `v` with `sin(x)`. Let me check which candidates can produce this.

Most candidates use terms like `v*x`, `v*x²`, `v*exp(c*x)`, etc. The question is: can any combination of these basis functions exactly reproduce `v*sin(x)` for all x?

**Key insight:** `sin(x)` has a Taylor series: `x - x³/3! + x⁵/5! - ...` which requires infinitely many polynomial terms. A finite polynomial in x (like `c*v*x + c*v*x²`) cannot equal `v*sin(x)`. Similarly, `v*exp(c*x)` is an exponential, not sinusoidal.

However, some candidates have `v*exp(c*x)` terms. Note that `exp(ix) = cos(x) + i*sin(x)`, but with real constants only, `exp(c*x)` cannot produce `sin(x)`.

Let me check if any combination of `v*x + v*x² + v*exp(c*x)` can equal `v*sin(x) + const*v` for all x. This would require `c3*x + c4*x² + c5*exp(c6*x) = sin(x) + const` for all x, which is impossible since the left side has exponential/polynomial basis functions while the right has a trigonometric function.

Similarly, `v*x⁴`, `v*cos(c*x)`, `v*log(...)`, `v*(c+x)^c`, `v*|v|*x²`, `v/(...)` cannot produce `v*sin(x)`.

Let me check **Candidate 35**: `c0 + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*x + c4*v*x + c5*v*x**2 + c6*v*exp(c7*x) + c8*v*cos(c9*x)`

This has `v*cos(c9*x)`. Setting `c9` appropriately: `cos(c9*x)` with a phase shift... but there's no phase constant inside the cosine of x. `cos(c9*x)` cannot equal `sin(x)` for all x (since `sin(x) = cos(x - π/2)`, we'd need `c9=1` and a phase shift, but there's no phase shift available in `cos(c9*x)`). So this doesn't work either.

**Candidate 48**: Has `v*exp(c*x)` and `v/(c+v²)^0.5` — neither produces `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidate 49**: Has `v*log(c*|x|+1)` — not `sin(x)`.

None of the candidates contain a `v*sin(x)` term or any combination of terms that could algebraically produce `v*sin(x)` exactly. The basis functions available (polynomials in x, exp(cx), log, |x|, Max, power functions) are all fundamentally different from sin(x) and cannot reproduce it exactly over the full domain.

Since `v*sin(x)` is an essential term in the GT (with a non-zero coefficient), and no candidate can produce this term, none of the candidates match.

Candidate 1 through 50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.
